# LoCoBench-Agent Task

## Overview

**Task ID**: java_api_rest_expert_006_architectural_understanding_expert_01
**Category**: architectural_understanding

**Context Length**: 778633 tokens

## Task Title

Architectural Analysis for a New Cross-Service Orchestration Feature

## Description

The OpsForge Utility Nexus is a complex microservices-based system designed to provide various backend utility functions. The architecture follows established patterns including an API Gateway for ingress, a Service Discovery registry, a centralized Config Server, and a shared common library for cross-cutting concerns. The individual microservices (e.g., `file-converter-service`, `data-anonymizer-service`) are built using a Hexagonal Architecture (Ports and Adapters), as documented in the project's ADRs. The system currently supports independent, synchronous REST calls and some asynchronous, event-driven interactions for specific services. A new business requirement has emerged to support complex, multi-step, asynchronous workflows that combine the capabilities of existing services.

## Your Task

You are a senior architect tasked with designing a solution for a new 'Data Processing Pipeline' feature. This feature must allow users to submit a job that executes a sequence of operations across multiple services. For example, a pipeline might first anonymize a dataset using the `data-anonymizer-service` and then convert the resulting data into a different format using the `file-converter-service`.

Your task is to produce a high-level architectural proposal. You are not required to write the full implementation, but you must demonstrate a deep understanding of the existing system to ensure your proposal is consistent and viable.

Your analysis must include:
1.  A brief summary of the current architecture's key components and communication patterns.
2.  A proposal for implementing the new 'Data Processing Pipeline' feature. Your proposal should address where the orchestration logic should live (e.g., in a new service or an existing one) and justify your choice by analyzing architectural trade-offs (e.g., Orchestration vs. Choreography).
3.  A detailed description of the data flow and component interactions for a sample pipeline job (e.g., Anonymize then Convert). This should cover the initial request, state management, inter-service communication, and how the final result is made available to the user.
4.  A list of the key new modules/files that would need to be created and a list of existing files that would require significant modification to implement your proposed design.

## Expected Approach

An expert developer would first seek to understand the macro- and micro-architectures of the system.

1.  **Macro-architecture Review:** The developer would start by examining `docker-compose.yml`, the root `pom.xml`, and the ADRs (`001-architectural-style-microservices.md`, `002-hexagonal-architecture-for-services.md`). This would reveal the microservice nature of the system, the key infrastructure components (API Gateway, Service Discovery, Config Server), and the overarching design philosophy.

2.  **Micro-architecture Deep Dive:** The developer would then inspect a representative service, like `file-converter-service`. They would analyze its `pom.xml` (dependencies), its configuration (`application.yml`, `bootstrap.yml`), and its source code structure. They would identify the Hexagonal Architecture implementation by looking at the `domain`, `adapter`, and `port` packages. They would note the existence of both inbound web adapters (`FileConversionController`) and inbound messaging adapters (`FileConversionMessageListener`), indicating the system handles both synchronous and asynchronous requests.

3.  **Design & Trade-off Analysis:** With this context, the developer would evaluate options for the new pipeline:
    *   **Choreography:** One service emits an event, and another service reacts to it. For a multi-step pipeline, this would create a chain of events (e.g., `AnonymizationComplete` event triggers the file converter). This is loosely coupled but makes the overall workflow implicit and hard to monitor or debug, especially for error handling (e.g., what if step 2 of 3 fails?).
    *   **Orchestration:** A central component actively manages the workflow, calling each service in sequence and handling the state. This is more tightly coupled to the workflow logic but makes the process explicit, easier to manage, monitor, and add complex logic like retries or compensation actions.

4.  **Conclusion:** For a defined, stateful, multi-step business process, orchestration is the superior pattern. The developer would propose creating a new `pipeline-orchestrator-service`.

5.  **Proposal Detailing:** The developer would then outline this new service. It would be a new Spring Boot application, follow the Hexagonal pattern, register with the service discovery, and pull from the config server. It would expose a REST endpoint for starting and monitoring jobs. Internally, its 'outbound adapters' would be HTTP clients responsible for communicating with the other utility services (anonymizer, converter, etc.). The developer would also detail the flow: a client gets a `jobId` back immediately, and the orchestrator service handles the long-running process, allowing the client to poll for status using the `jobId`.

## Evaluation Criteria

- **Component Identification:** Correctly identifies the roles of the API Gateway, Service Discovery, Config Server, and individual microservices.
- **Pattern Recognition:** Explicitly recognizes and references the Microservices and Hexagonal Architecture patterns guiding the system's design.
- **Architectural Trade-off Analysis:** Accurately discusses the pros and cons of Orchestration vs. Choreography in the context of this specific problem.
- **Solution Cohesion:** Proposes a solution (the new service) that aligns with the existing architectural patterns (Hexagonal, uses discovery/config) rather than introducing a conflicting design.
- **Impact Analysis:** Correctly identifies the need for a new service module and pinpoints the key existing files (`pom.xml`, `GatewayRouteConfig.java`, `docker-compose.yml`) that must be modified.
- **Flow Description:** Provides a clear, logical, and technically sound description of the end-to-end data flow for the new feature, including its asynchronous nature.

     1→# 001 – Architectural Style: Microservices
     2→
     3→Status: **Accepted**  
     4→Date: 2023-08-29  
     5→ADR-Owner: Architecture Guild  
     6→
     7→---
     8→
     9→## 1. Context
    10→
    11→OpsForge Utility Nexus aims to provide a *single, versioned façade* that aggregates a wide variety of utilities—file-format conversion, data anonymisation, checksum generation, time-zone-aware scheduling, etc. Each utility has a distinct lifecycle, scalability profile, and set of external dependencies.
    12→
    13→Historically, similar platforms have been built as:
    14→
    15→* a **monolith**, offering a single deployment artefact, or  
    16→* a **modular monolith**, separating code at compile-time while sharing the same runtime and database schema.
    17→
    18→Early spike implementations revealed several pain-points:
    19→
    20→* **Resource Contention** – CPU-intensive converters starved IO-bound schedulers.  
    21→* **Release Cadence Mismatch** – checksum algorithms evolve slowly; anonymisation libraries update weekly.  
    22→* **Polyglot Dependencies** – some utilities require native binaries; others depend on JDBC drivers.  
    23→* **Regulatory Isolation** – GDPR mandates data-anonymisation modules to undergo specific audits, blocking the entire delivery pipeline.
    24→
    25→Given these concerns—and the fact that customers frequently request *only one or two* utilities—we need an architectural style that supports:
    26→
    27→* Independent release and deployment cadences  
    28→* Autonomous horizontal scaling  
    29→* Technology heterogeneity per utility  
    30→* Fine-grained security boundaries  
    31→* Evolutionary replacement of utilities without cross-cutting regression risk  
    32→
    33→## 2. Decision
    34→

17-usertool_resultRead
     1→```md
     2→# 002 — Hexagonal Architecture for Services
     3→> Status: **Accepted**  
     4→> Date: 2024-06-16  
     5→> Decision Makers: Platform Architecture Guild  
     6→> Supersedes: N/A  
     7→> Tags: architecture, hexagonal, ports-and-adapters
     8→
     9→## 1. Context
    10→OpsForge Utility Nexus exposes a suite of *utility micro-services* ranging from file conversions to bulk text transformations.  
    11→We need each service to be:
    12→
    13→* Technology-agnostic at its core  
    14→* Swappable in-/out-bound infrastructure without touching business logic  
    15→* Meticulously testable (pure unit tests at the core, integration tests at the edges)  
    16→* Compatible with both HTTP/JSON and GraphQL façades  
    17→
    18→These goals naturally align with **Hexagonal Architecture (aka Ports & Adapters)**.
    19→
    20→## 2. Decision
    21→Every utility is implemented as a self-contained hexagon:
    22→
    23→1. **Domain/Core**  
    24→   * Pure POJOs and value objects  
    25→   * Use-case orchestrators (Application Services)  
    26→   * Port interfaces (inbound & outbound)
    27→
    28→2. **Adapters**  
    29→   * **Inbound**: REST controllers / GraphQL resolvers / message listeners  
    30→   * **Outbound**: Repository drivers, SaaS connectors, cache providers  
    31→
    32→3. **Configuration**  
    33→   * Wiring of ports to adapters via dependency injection (Spring Boot)  
    34→   * Uniform, versioned contracts exposed by the API Gateway layer  
    35→
    36→All cross-cutting concerns (rate limiting, caching, tracing, etc.) are expressed as *decorators* or *framework interceptors*, never leaking into domain code.
    37→
    38→## 3. Consequences
    39→✔ Fast unit tests against core logic  
    40→✔ Easy to
... (truncated)

    11→
    12→## Status
    13→Accepted – supersedes ADR-001 “Experimental Gateway PoC”.  
    14→This decision is **binding** for all utility verticals (conversion, anonymization, scheduling, checksums, text-ops) starting with platform version **v1.2.0**.
    15→
    16→---
    17→
    18→## Context
    19→
    20→OpsForge Utility Nexus aspires to expose a single, coherent contract while allowing each utility to remain an independent, hexagonally-structured microservice.  
    21→A façade layer (a.k.a. “API Gateway”) must therefore:
    22→
    23→* Expose **stable, consumer-centric endpoints** that abstract internal topology changes.  
    24→* Support **REST _and_ GraphQL** entry points without duplicating business logic.  
    25→* Enforce **cross-cutting concerns** (rate limiting, authN/Z, tenant routing, observability, caching).  
    26→* Provide **versioning guarantees** that enable non-breaking evolution.  
    27→* Remain **agnostic** of the utilities’ programming language, transport protocol or data store.
    28→
    29→Early prototypes evaluated three approaches:
    30→
    31→| # | Approach | Pros | Cons |
    32→|---|----------|------|------|
    33→| A | Pass-through API Gateway (e.g. NGINX + Lua) | Low latency; infra-centric | Lacks domain validation; brittle error handling; Lua skillset scarcity |
    34→| B | “Thin” GraphQL BFF per client | Flexible composition; schema-driven | Code duplication across BFFs; N+1 requests; operational overhead |
    35→| C | Unified **Java** façade runni

94-assistanttext-
I have completed the architectural analysis and written a comprehensive solution to `/logs/agent/solution.md`. Here's a summary of what was accomplished:

## Summary

### 1. Current Architecture Analysis
- Identified key infrastructure components: **API Gateway**, **Service Discovery** (Eureka), **Config Server**, and **Common Library**
- Mapped all utility microservices: File Converter, Data Anonymizer, Checksum Generator, Scheduler, and Text Transformer
- Confirmed the system follows **Microservices Architecture** (ADR-001) and **Hexagonal Architecture** (ADR-002)
- Found both synchronous REST and asynchronous Kafka communication patterns in use

### 2. Architectural Trade-off Analysis
- Compared **Choreography** vs **Orchestration** patterns for multi-step workflows
- Recommended **Orchestration** because:
  - Explicit workflow visibility
  - Centralized state management
  - Easier error handling and compensation
  - Better monitoring capabilities

### 3. Proposed Solution: `pipeline-orchestrator-service`
A new microservice that:
- Follows existing Hexagonal Architecture patterns
- Registers with Service Discovery
- Pulls configuration from Config Server
- Exposes REST endpoints for job submission and status queries
- Uses HTTP clients to call downstream services (anonymizer, converter)
- Persists job state to PostgreSQL

### 4. Detailed Data Flow
Documented the complete flow for an "Anonymize-then-Convert" pipeline:
1. Client submits job → immediate `202 Accepted` with job ID
2. Orchestrator executes Step 1 (Anonymization)
3. Stores intermediate result
4. Orchestrator executes Step 2 (Conversion)
5. Stores final result, marks job complete
6. Client polls for status and downloads result

### 5. Impact Analysis
**New Files:**
- Complete `pipeline-orchestrator-service`

  "file": {
    "content": "# 001 \u2013 Architectural Style: Microservices\n\nStatus: **Accepted**  \nDate: 2023-08-29  \nADR-Owner: Architecture Guild  \n\n---\n\n## 1. Context\n\nOpsForge Utility Nexus aims to provide a *single, versioned fa\u00e7ade* that aggregates a wide variety of utilities\u2014file-format conversion, data anonymisation, checksum generation, time-zone-aware scheduling, etc. Each utility has a distinct lifecycle, scalability profile, and set of external dependencies.\n\nHistorically, similar platforms have been built as:\n\n* a **monolith**, offering a single deployment artefact, or  \n* a **modular monolith**, separating code at compile-time while sharing the same runtime and database schema.\n\nEarly spike implementations revealed several pain-points:\n\n* **Resource Contention** \u2013 CPU-intensive converters starved IO-bound schedulers.  \n* **Release Cadence Mismatch** \u2013 checksum algorithms evolve slowly; anonymisation libraries update weekly.  \n* **Polyglot Dependencies** \u2013 some utilities require native binaries; others depend on JDBC drivers.  \n* **Regulatory Isolation** \u2013 GDPR mandates data-anonymisation modules to undergo specific audits, blocking the entire delivery pipeline.\n\nGiven these concerns\u2014and the fact that customers frequently request *only one or two* utilities\u2014we need an architectural style that supports:\n\n* Independent release and deployment cadences  \n* Autonomous horizontal scaling  \n* Technology heterogeneity per utility  \n* Fine-grained security boundaries  \n* Evolutionary replacement of utilities without cross-cutting regression risk  \n\n## 2. Decision\n\nWe will architect OpsForge Utility Nexus as a **Microservice-oriented System**, in which *each utility function is implemented as its own microservice* that:\n\n1. Exposes its capabilities via a lightweight REST and (optionally) GraphQL API.  \n2. Owns its **hexagonal architecture** internals\u2014domain, application services, inbound/outbound adapters.  \n3. Communicates with other services only through well-defined, versioned contracts (HTTP/JSON and/or gRPC where streaming is required).  \n4. Publishes domain events on an event bus for eventual consistency and observability.  \n5. Is deployed, scaled, and monitored independently, yet discovered and composed by the **API Gateway** to present a cohesive fa\u00e7ade to consumers.\n\n### Illustrative Directory Layout\n\n```text\nopsforge-utility-nexus/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 gateway/               # Spring Cloud Gateway + GraphQL Federation\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 utilities/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 checksum/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 converter/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 anonymizer/\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 scheduler/\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 shared-kernel/         # Value objects, error codes, cross-service contracts\n```\n\n### Minimal Service Contract Example (Checksum Utility)\n\n```java\n// inbound adapter\n@RestController\n@RequestMapping(\"/v1/checksum\")\n@RequiredArgsConstructor\nclass ChecksumController {\n\n    private final ChecksumUseCase checksumUseCase;\n\n    @PostMapping\n    ResponseEntity<ChecksumResponse> calculate(@Valid @RequestBody ChecksumRequest request) {\n        ChecksumResult result = checksumUseCase.calculate(request.toDomain());\n        return ResponseEntity.ok(ChecksumResponse.from(result));\n    }\n}\n```\n\n## 3. Rationale\n\n* **Decoupled Deployment** \u2013 Teams push features without synchronising global release trains.  \n* **Scalability Alignment** \u2013 CPU-bound converters can autoscale independently of latency-sensitive schedulers.  \n* **Failure Containment** \u2013 Circuit-breaking a malfunctioning anonymisation service leaves other utilities unaffected.  \n* **Technology Freedom** \u2013 Teams may select optimal persistence (e.g., PostgreSQL vs MongoDB) or caching layers (e.g., Caffeine vs Redis) without impacting peers.  \n* **Regulatory Compliance** \u2013 Security reviews and audits can scope to the service that touches sensitive data.\n\n## 4. Consequences\n\nPros:\n\n* Faster, risk-isolated releases  \n* Resilience via bulkheads, retries, timeouts  \n* Fine-grained autoscaling, leading to cost optimisation  \n* Facilitates domain-driven design and bounded contexts  \n\nCons / Trade-offs:\n\n* **Operational Overhead** \u2013 More CI pipelines, Docker images, Helm charts, dashboards, alerts.  \n* **Distributed Complexity** \u2013 Requires centralised logging, tracing, service discovery, and advanced DevSecOps maturity.  \n* **Data Consistency** \u2013 Cross-service transactions demand eventual consistency or Saga patterns.  \n* **Cross-Cutting Concerns Duplication** \u2013 Rate-limiting, auth, and caching must be standardised via libraries or sidecars.\n\nMitigations:\n\n* Provide a **Golden Path** with base images, Terraform modules, Helm templates, and shared Gradle plugins.  \n* Adopt **OpenTelemetry** for unified traces, metrics, and logs.  \n* Leverage **GraphQL Federation** to stitch service schemas and reduce REST round-trips.  \n* Enforce **Semantic Versioning** and **Consumer-Driven Contract Tests** (Pact) to detect breaking changes early.\n\n## 5. Alternatives Considered\n\n| Candidate                      | Why Rejected                                                                 |\n|--------------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------|\n| Monolith                       | Single blast radius; divergent scalability needs cause over-provisioning     |\n| Modular Monolith               | Better boundaries than classic monolith, but still shares runtime & DB       |\n| Functions-as-a-Service (FaaS)  | Cold-start latency unacceptable for bulk conversions; complex orchestration  |\n| Self-contained Systems (SCS)   | Similar benefits but less tooling support compared to mainstream microservices |\n\n## 6. Related Decisions\n\n* 002 \u2013 **Hexagonal Architecture Enforcement**  \n* 003 \u2013 **API Gateway & GraphQL Federation Strategy**  \n* 004 \u2013 **Event Streaming Backbone (Kafka)**  \n* 005 \u2013 **Observability Stack Selection**  \n\n---\n\n> *This ADR is irrevocable only as long as its motivation remains valid. Should empirical evidence prove otherwise, it may be superseded following established governance procedures.*",
    "filePath": "/app/project/docs/adr/001-architectural-style-microservices.md",

    "content": "```md\n# 002\u200a\u2014\u200aHexagonal Architecture for Services\n> Status: **Accepted**  \n> Date: 2024-06-16  \n> Decision Makers: Platform Architecture Guild  \n> Supersedes: N/A  \n> Tags: architecture, hexagonal, ports-and-adapters\n\n## 1. Context\nOpsForge Utility Nexus exposes a suite of *utility micro-services* ranging from file conversions to bulk text transformations.  \nWe need each service to be:\n\n* Technology-agnostic at its core  \n* Swappable in-/out-bound infrastructure without touching business logic  \n* Meticulously testable (pure unit tests at the core, integration tests at the edges)  \n* Compatible with both HTTP/JSON and GraphQL fa\u00e7ades  \n\nThese goals naturally align with **Hexagonal Architecture (aka Ports & Adapters)**.\n\n## 2. Decision\nEvery utility is implemented as a self-contained hexagon:\n\n1. **Domain/Core**  \n   * Pure POJOs and value objects  \n   * Use-case orchestrators (Application Services)  \n   * Port interfaces (inbound & outbound)\n\n2. **Adapters**  \n   * **Inbound**: REST controllers / GraphQL resolvers / message listeners  \n   * **Outbound**: Repository drivers, SaaS connectors, cache providers  \n\n3. **Configuration**  \n   * Wiring of ports to adapters via dependency injection (Spring Boot)  \n   * Uniform, versioned contracts exposed by the API Gateway layer  \n\nAll cross-cutting concerns (rate limiting, caching, tracing, etc.) are expressed as *decorators* or *framework interceptors*, never leaking into domain code.\n\n## 3. Consequences\n\u2714 Fast unit tests against core logic  \n\u2714 Easy to swap technologies (e.g., Caffeine \u2192 Redis)  \n\u2714 Clear test boundaries (mock ports instead of mocks everywhere)  \n\u2718 Slightly higher initial boilerplate (worth the ROI)\n\n---\n\n## 4. Reference Implementation\n\nBelow is a trimmed, yet **runnable** example of the File-Conversion utility adopting the hexagonal style.\n\n```java\n// -------- 1\ufe0f\u20e3 Domain Layer (Core) -------------------------------------------\npackage com.opsforge.utility.fileconversion.domain;\n\nimport java.time.OffsetDateTime;\nimport java.util.UUID;\n\n/**\n * Value object that represents a single file-conversion request.\n */\npublic record ConversionRequest(\n        UUID requestId,\n        String sourceFormat,\n        String targetFormat,\n        byte[] payload,\n        OffsetDateTime requestedAt\n) {}\n\n/**\n * Port that expresses the *purpose* of persisting conversion artefacts.\n */\npublic interface ArtefactStoragePort {\n    void save(UUID requestId, byte[] convertedPayload);\n}\n\n/**\n * Primary use-case orchestrator (Application Service).\n */\npublic class ConvertFileUseCase {\n\n    private final ArtefactStoragePort storagePort;\n    private final FileFormatConverter converter; // pure domain service\n\n    public ConvertFileUseCase(ArtefactStoragePort storagePort,\n                              FileFormatConverter converter) {\n        this.storagePort = storagePort;\n        this.converter   = converter;\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Executes the conversion and persists the output using the outbound port.\n     */\n    public ConversionResponse execute(ConversionRequest request) {\n        byte[] output = converter.convert(\n                request.sourceFormat(),\n                request.targetFormat(),\n                request.payload()\n        );\n        storagePort.save(request.requestId(), output);\n        return new ConversionResponse(request.requestId(), output.length);\n    }\n}\n\n/**\n * Domain service that performs format conversion.\n * Decoupled from any IO concerns.\n */\npublic interface FileFormatConverter {\n    byte[] convert(String from, String to, byte[] input);\n}\n\n/**\n * Minimal response DTO emitted by the use-case.\n */\npublic record ConversionResponse(UUID requestId, int sizeInBytes) {}\n```\n\n```java\n// -------- 2\ufe0f\u20e3 Inbound Adapter (REST Controller) -----------------------------\npackage com.opsforge.utility.fileconversion.inbound.rest;\n\nimport com.opsforge.utility.fileconversion.domain.*;\nimport jakarta.validation.constraints.NotNull;\nimport org.springframework.http.ResponseEntity;\nimport org.springframework.validation.annotation.Validated;\nimport org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.*;\n\nimport java.time.OffsetDateTime;\nimport java.util.UUID;\n\n/**\n * REST fa\u00e7ade that delegates to the core use-case.\n */\n@RestController\n@RequestMapping(\"/v1/conversions\")\n@Validated\npublic class FileConversionController {\n\n    private final ConvertFileUseCase useCase;\n\n    public FileConversionController(ConvertFileUseCase useCase) {\n        this.useCase = useCase;\n    }\n\n    @PostMapping\n    public ResponseEntity<ConversionResponse> convert(\n            @RequestParam @NotNull String sourceFormat,\n            @RequestParam @NotNull String targetFormat,\n            @RequestBody byte[] payload\n    ) {\n        ConversionRequest request = new ConversionRequest(\n                UUID.randomUUID(),\n                sourceFormat,\n                targetFormat,\n                payload,\n                OffsetDateTime.now()\n        );\n        return ResponseEntity.ok(useCase.execute(request));\n    }\n}\n```\n\n```java\n// -------- 3\ufe0f\u20e3 Outbound Adapter (S3 Artefact Storage) ------------------------\npackage com.opsforge.utility.fileconversion.outbound.s3;\n\nimport com.opsforge.utility.fileconversion.domain.ArtefactStoragePort;\nimport org.slf4j.Logger;\nimport org.slf4j.LoggerFactory;\nimport software.amazon.awssdk.core.sync.RequestBody;\nimport software.amazon.awssdk.services.s3.S3Client;\nimport software.amazon.awssdk.services.s3.model.PutObjectRequest;\n\nimport java.util.UUID;\n\n/**\n * Concrete adapter that stores conversion outputs in an S3 bucket.\n */\npublic class S3ArtefactStorageAdapter implements ArtefactStoragePort {\n\n    private static final Logger LOG = LoggerFactory.getLogger(S3ArtefactStorageAdapter.class);\n\n    private final S3Client s3;\n    private final String   bucketName;\n\n    public S3ArtefactStorageAdapter(S3Client s3, String bucketName) {\n        this.s3 = s3;\n        this.bucketName = bucketName;\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void save(UUID requestId, byte[] convertedPayload) {\n        try {\n            PutObjectRequest req = PutObjectRequest.builder()\n                    .bucket(bucketName)\n                    .key(requestId + \".bin\")\n                    .build();\n            s3.putObject(req, RequestBody.fromBytes(convertedPayload));\n        } catch (Exception e) {\n            LOG.error(\"Failed to store artefact for request {}\", requestId, e);\n            throw new ArtefactStorageException(requestId, e);\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n```java\n// -------- 4\ufe0f\u20e3 Configuration (Spring) ---------------------------------------\npackage com.opsforge.utility.fileconversion.config;\n\nimport com.opsforge.utility.fileconversion.domain.*;\nimport com.opsforge.utility.fileconversion.outbound.s3.S3ArtefactStorageAdapter;\nimport org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.condition.ConditionalOnProperty;\nimport org.springframework.context.annotation.Bean;\nimport org.springframework.context.annotation.Configuration;\nimport software.amazon.awssdk.services.s3.S3Client;\n\n/**\n * Wires ports to adapters using Spring\u2019s DI container.\n */\n@Configuration\npublic class FileConversionModule {\n\n    @Bean\n    ConvertFileUseCase convertFileUseCase(\n            ArtefactStoragePort storagePort,\n            FileFormatConverter converter) {\n        return new ConvertFileUseCase(storagePort, converter);\n    }\n\n    @Bean\n    @ConditionalOnProperty(name = \"storage.provider\", havingValue = \"s3\")\n    ArtefactStoragePort s3StoragePort(S3Client s3,\n                                      FileConversionProperties props) {\n        return new S3ArtefactStorageAdapter(s3, props.bucket());\n    }\n}\n```\n\n```java\n// -------- 5\ufe0f\u20e3 Cross-Cutting Concern (Caching Decorator) --------------------\npackage com.opsforge.utility.fileconversion.outbound.cache;\n\nimport com.github.benmanes.caffeine.cache.Cache;\nimport com.opsforge.utility.fileconversion.domain.ArtefactStoragePort;\n\nimport java.util.UUID;\n\n/**\n * Transparently caches artefacts before delegating to the \"real\" port.\n */\npublic class CachingStorageDecorator implements ArtefactStoragePort {\n\n    private final Cache<UUID, byte[]> cache;\n    private final ArtefactStoragePort delegate;\n\n    public CachingStorageDecorator(Cache<UUID, byte[]> cache,\n                                   ArtefactStoragePort delegate) {\n        this.cache = cache;\n        this.delegate = delegate;\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void save(UUID requestId, byte[] convertedPayload) {\n        cache.put(requestId, convertedPayload);\n        delegate.save(requestId, convertedPayload);\n    }\n}\n```\n\n## 5. Testing Strategy\n* **Core tests**: Pure JUnit tests verifying `ConvertFileUseCase` with mocked ports  \n* **Adapter tests**: Web-layer tests for controller, TestContainers for S3 emulation  \n* **Contract tests**: Swagger / GraphQL SDL snapshots per version\n\n---\n\n## 6. Rejected Alternatives\n1. Layered (n-tier) architecture \u2014 tight coupling across layers, harder to swap tech.  \n2. Anemic-model approach \u2014 domain logic scattered in services, violates DDD principles.  \n\n---\n\n## 7. Links\n* Alistair Cockburn, *Hexagonal Architecture* (2005)  \n* Fowler, *Ports and Adapters* article  \n```\n",

    "content": "```markdown\n<!--\n  OpsForge Utility Nexus \u2013 ADR 003\n  Title: API Fa\u00e7ade Strategy\n  Status: Accepted\n  Date: 2024-04-27\n  Deciders: @arch-lead, @api-lead, @infra-lead\n-->\n\n# 003 \u2013 API Fa\u00e7ade Strategy\n\n## Status\nAccepted \u2013 supersedes ADR-001 \u201cExperimental Gateway PoC\u201d.  \nThis decision is **binding** for all utility verticals (conversion, anonymization, scheduling, checksums, text-ops) starting with platform version **v1.2.0**.\n\n---\n\n## Context\n\nOpsForge Utility Nexus aspires to expose a single, coherent contract while allowing each utility to remain an independent, hexagonally-structured microservice.  \nA fa\u00e7ade layer (a.k.a. \u201cAPI Gateway\u201d) must therefore:\n\n* Expose **stable, consumer-centric endpoints** that abstract internal topology changes.  \n* Support **REST _and_ GraphQL** entry points without duplicating business logic.  \n* Enforce **cross-cutting concerns** (rate limiting, authN/Z, tenant routing, observability, caching).  \n* Provide **versioning guarantees** that enable non-breaking evolution.  \n* Remain **agnostic** of the utilities\u2019 programming language, transport protocol or data store.\n\nEarly prototypes evaluated three approaches:\n\n| # | Approach | Pros | Cons |\n|---|----------|------|------|\n| A | Pass-through API Gateway (e.g. NGINX + Lua) | Low latency; infra-centric | Lacks domain validation; brittle error handling; Lua skillset scarcity |\n| B | \u201cThin\u201d GraphQL BFF per client | Flexible composition; schema-driven | Code duplication across BFFs; N+1 requests; operational overhead |\n| C | Unified **Java** fa\u00e7ade running in the same tech stack as utilities | Reuse common libs; type safety; Spring/WebFlux maturity | Increases JVM footprint; may appear monolithic |\n\nEmpirical load-tests and maintainability reviews highlighted option **C** as the most sustainable: it maximises code reuse (error model, pagination, DTO mappers) and minimises operational sprawl.\n\n---\n\n## Decision\n\nWe will implement a **unified Java-based fa\u00e7ade service** that:\n\n1. Uses **Spring Boot 3.2** with **WebFlux** for non-blocking HTTP and **Netflix DGS** for GraphQL.\n2. Implements **API-First** workflow via **OpenAPI 3.1** and **GraphQL SDL** living in `contracts/`.\n3. Delegates all business logic to downstream utilities through **dedicated outbound ports** (Feign Client interfaces for REST, gRPC stubs, or JMS templates).\n4. Applies **API versioning** through\n   * URI segment (`/v{n}/\u2026`) for REST  \n   * Namespaced GraphQL schema (`schema @tag(name:\"v{n}\")`) for GraphQL\n5. Encapsulates **cross-cutting filters** (auth, rate-limit, metrics, cache) using Spring `WebFilter` / `HandlerInterceptor` and DGS `DataFetcherInterceptor`.\n6. Emits **structured problem details** (`application/problem+json`) conforming to [RFC 9457] for error handling.\n7. Offers **partial responses & pagination** (RFC 7240 / Cursor-based) out of the box.\n\n---\n\n## Consequences\n\n### Positive\n* **Consistency** \u2013 All clients (CLI, SDKs, UI) leverage the same semantics, reducing cognitive load.\n* **Evolutionary** \u2013 Internals can migrate (REST \u2192 gRPC; Caffeine \u2192 Redis) without public contract churn.\n* **Observability** \u2013 Central fa\u00e7ade surfaces unified logs, tracing, and metrics, expediting SRE workflows.\n* **Security** \u2013 Single choke-point to enforce JWT scopes, multi-tenancy guards, and threat mitigations.\n\n### Negative / Mitigations\n* **Increased Blast Radius** \u2013 A defect in the fa\u00e7ade could affect all utilities.  \n  \u2192 Mitigation: Blue/Green deploys, exhaustive test pyramid, layered health-checks.\n* **Throughput Bottleneck** \u2013 Additional hop may introduce latency.  \n  \u2192 Mitigation: WebFlux back-pressure, response caching, and gRPC multiplexing for chatty paths.\n* **Perceived Monolith** \u2013 May obscure microservice boundaries.  \n  \u2192 Mitigation: Maintain clear ownership docs, contract tests, and align domain events per utility.\n\n---\n\n## Alternatives Considered\n\n* **GraphQL Federation** \u2013 Rejected due to premature complexity and lack of per-utility SDL maturity.\n* **Service Mesh Sidecars** (Istio, Linkerd) \u2013 Suitable for transport-level concerns but insufficient for domain validation and versioning semantics.\n* **Serverless Edge Functions** \u2013 Would optimise global latency but complicate stateful retries and bulk payload handling (>10 MB).\n\n---\n\n## Compliance & Reference Implementation\n\nAll new endpoints **MUST**:\n\n1. Conform to the published OpenAPI/GraphQL contract before merge.  \n2. Return a `problem+json` body for 4xx/5xx categories.  \n3. Include `X-Request-Id`, `X-Correlation-Id` in all egress calls.  \n4. Register with the fa\u00e7ade\u2019s central `UtilityRegistry` during application bootstrap.\n\nReference code lives in `opsforge-facade/src/main/java/.../facade`.  \nSample usage:\n\n```java\n@GetMapping(path = \"/v1/checksums/sha256\", produces = APPLICATION_JSON_VALUE)\npublic Mono<ChecksumResponse> calculateSha256(@Valid ChecksumRequest req) {\n    return checksumPort.calculate(req)\n                       .map(mapper::toResponse)\n                       .timeout(Duration.ofSeconds(5))\n                       .onErrorMap(TimeoutException.class, ProblemDetails::fromTimeout);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Next Steps\n\n1. Finalise fa\u00e7ade v1 contract freeze (2024-05-15).\n2. Migrate existing CLI to new endpoints.\n3. Deprecate NGINX Lua scripts by Q3.\n\n---\n\n### Changelog\n* 2024-04-27 \u2013 Initial decision recorded.\n```\n",

    "content": "package com.opsforge.nexus.fileconverter.domain.port.in;\n\nimport java.nio.ByteBuffer;\nimport java.nio.file.Path;\nimport java.time.Instant;\nimport java.util.Collections;\nimport java.util.Map;\nimport java.util.Objects;\nimport java.util.Optional;\nimport java.util.UUID;\n\n/**\n * Incoming (primary) port that describes the use-cases the File Converter domain\n * exposes to the outside world (e.g. REST controllers, GraphQL resolvers,\n * asynchronous message listeners). <p>\n *\n * The interface is intentionally technology-agnostic and free of any framework\n * dependencies so that the core domain remains portable and fully testable.\n *\n * Implementations live in the {@code application} layer and are wired to\n * outbound ports (secondary adapters) that perform the actual I/O work, such as\n * reading the source file from a blob store or delegating the conversion to an\n * external SaaS.\n */\npublic interface FileConversionUseCase {\n\n    /**\n     * Creates a new conversion job. Depending on the implementation this call\n     * may be synchronous or queue an asynchronous background task.\n     *\n     * @param command immutable command that carries all data required to start\n     *                a conversion\n     * @return unique immutable {@link ConversionJobId}\n     * @throws UnsupportedFileFormatException when either source or target\n     *                                        format is not supported by the\n     *                                        current deployment\n     */\n    ConversionJobId submitConversion(ConvertFileCommand command)\n            throws UnsupportedFileFormatException;\n\n    /**\n     * Returns the current status of a conversion job.\n     *\n     * @param jobId unique job identifier as returned by\n     *              {@link #submitConversion(ConvertFileCommand)}\n     * @return {@link ConversionSnapshot} carrying status and additional metadata\n     * @throws JobNotFoundException when the job cannot be located\n     */\n    ConversionSnapshot queryStatus(ConversionJobId jobId) throws JobNotFoundException;\n\n    /**\n     * Retrieves the converted payload as a binary buffer <strong>if and only\n     * if</strong> the job has successfully completed. Implementations may\n     * decide to stream large files; this simplified interface suffices for most\n     * cases.\n     *\n     * @param jobId unique identifier of a completed job\n     * @return optional containing the payload or empty when the job is not yet\n     *         finished\n     * @throws JobNotFoundException               when the job cannot be located\n     * @throws ConversionFailedException          when the job finished in\n     *                                            {@link ConversionStatus#FAILED}\n     * @throws UnsupportedRetrievalStateException when the job is not in a state\n     *                                            that allows retrieval\n     */\n    Optional<ByteBuffer> fetchConvertedPayload(ConversionJobId jobId)\n            throws JobNotFoundException,\n                   ConversionFailedException,\n                   UnsupportedRetrievalStateException;\n\n    /**\n     * Attempts to cancel an in-flight conversion. A best-effort operation;\n     * implementations must guarantee idempotency.\n     *\n     * @param jobId job to cancel\n     * @throws JobNotFoundException            when the job cannot be located\n     * @throws ConversionAlreadyCompletedException when the job is already in a\n     *                                            terminal state\n     */\n    void cancelConversion(ConversionJobId jobId)\n            throws JobNotFoundException, ConversionAlreadyCompletedException;\n}\n\n/* ========================================================================== */\n/* ===============================  Commands  =============================== */\n/* ========================================================================== */\n\n/**\n * Immutable command object that starts a new conversion. Acts as the formal\n * boundary between primary adapters and the application service.\n */\nfinal class ConvertFileCommand {\n\n    private final Path sourcePath;\n    private final FileFormat sourceFormat;\n    private final FileFormat targetFormat;\n    private final Map<String, String> metadata; // arbitrary key-value data\n\n    private ConvertFileCommand(Builder builder) {\n        this.sourcePath   = builder.sourcePath;\n        this.sourceFormat = builder.sourceFormat;\n        this.targetFormat = builder.targetFormat;\n        this.metadata     = Collections.unmodifiableMap(builder.metadata);\n    }\n\n    public Path getSourcePath() {\n        return sourcePath;\n    }\n\n    public FileFormat getSourceFormat() {\n        return sourceFormat;\n    }\n\n    public FileFormat getTargetFormat() {\n        return targetFormat;\n    }\n\n    public Map<String, String> getMetadata() {\n        return metadata;\n    }\n\n    /* --------------------------  Builder pattern  -------------------------- */\n\n    public static Builder builder() {\n        return new Builder();\n    }\n\n    public static final class Builder {\n        private Path sourcePath;\n        private FileFormat sourceFormat;\n        private FileFormat targetFormat;\n        private Map<String, String> metadata = Collections.emptyMap();\n\n        private Builder() {\n        }\n\n        public Builder sourcePath(Path sourcePath) {\n            this.sourcePath = sourcePath;\n            return this;\n        }\n\n        public Builder sourceFormat(FileFormat sourceFormat) {\n            this.sourceFormat = sourceFormat;\n            return this;\n        }\n\n        public Builder targetFormat(FileFormat targetFormat) {\n            this.targetFormat = targetFormat;\n            return this;\n        }\n\n        public Builder metadata(Map<String, String> metadata) {\n            this.metadata = metadata == null ? Collections.emptyMap() : metadata;\n            return this;\n        }\n\n        public ConvertFileCommand build() {\n            Objects.requireNonNull(sourcePath,   \"sourcePath must not be null\");\n            Objects.requireNonNull(sourceFormat, \"sourceFormat must not be null\");\n            Objects.requireNonNull(targetFormat, \"targetFormat must not be null\");\n            return new ConvertFileCommand(this);\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/* ========================================================================== */\n/* ==============================  Value Objects      this.objectMapper          = objectMapper;\n        this.resultsTopic          = resultsTopic;\n\n        /*  Idempotency cache: protects against redeliveries within a time window.\n            Caffeine is light-weight and performs very well under high concurrency. */\n        this.processedMessageCache = Caffeine.newBuilder()\n                                             .expireAfterWrite(Duration.ofMinutes(deduplicationTtlMinutes))\n                                             .maximumSize(20_000)\n                                             .build();\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Main Kafka entry point. complete.\n     */\n    @KafkaListener(\n            topics = \"${nexus.messaging.topics.file-conversion-requests}\",\n            groupId = \"${spring.kafka.consumer.group-id}\",\n            final Consumer<?, ?> consumer) {\n\n        final String jobId  = record.key();   // jobId is used as Kafka key for natural ordering\n        final String payload = record.value();\n\n        /* ===== De-duplication ============================================================ */\n        if (processedMessageCache.getIfPresent(jobId) != null) {\n            log.info(\"Duplicate message objectMapper.readValue(payload, FileConversionRequestMessage.class);\n\n            /* ===== Validation ============================================================ */\n        return;\n            }\n\n            /* ===== Mapping DTO -> Domain Command ======================================== */\n            ConversionJobCommand command = .sourceFormat(requestDto.getSourceFormat())\n                                                               .targetFormat(requestDto.getTargetFormat())\n                                                               .originalFilename(requestDto.getOriginalFilename())\n                                                               .base64EncodedFile(requestDto.getBase64EncodedFile())\n                                                               .useLosslessCompression(requestDto.isUseLosslessCompression())\n                                                               .build();\n\n            /* ===== Invoke Use-Case ======================================================= */\n            ConversionJobResult conversionResult = fileConversionUseCase.convertFile(command);\n\n            /* ===== Publish Success Result =============================================== */\n            publishSuccess(conversionResult);\n\n            /* ===== Record processed message & commit offset ============================= */\n            processedMessageCache.put(jobId, Boolean.TRUE);\n            ack.acknowledge();\n\n            log.info(\"File-conversion job {} processed successfully\", jobId);\n\n        } catch (InvalidFormatException | JsonProcessingException e) {\n            log.error(\"Unable to deserialize message with key={}\", jobId, e);\n            publishFailure(jobId, ERROR_CODE_DESERIALIZATION, e.getOriginalMessage());\n            ack.acknowledge(); // Commit so we don't get stuck on poison pill\n        } catch (Exception e) {\n            log.error(\"Unexpected                id,\n                    dto.name(),\n                    host,\n                    dto.port(),\n                    dto.basePath(),\n                    Instant.now(),\n */\n\n        @CacheEvict(value = \"registryList\", allEntries = true)\n        public void deregister(UUID id) {\n            RegisteredService removed = store.remove(id);\n            if (removed == !s.isExpired());\n            if (serviceName.isPresent()) {\n                stream = stream.filter(s -> s.name().equalsIgnoreCase(serviceName.get()));\n            }\n            return stream.sorted(Comparator.comparing(RegisteredService::registeredAt).reversed())\n                         .collect(Collectors.toList());\n        }\n\n        public RegisteredService findById(UUID id) {\n            RegisteredService service = store.get(id);\n            if (service == null || service.isExpired()) {\n                throw new ServiceNotFoundException(\"No active service store.entrySet().removeIf(entry -> now.isAfter(entry.getValue().registeredAt().plus(entry.getValue().ttl())));\n        }\n\n        /* ---------------- Utilities ------------------- */\n\n            return ResponseEntity.status(NOT_FOUND).body(problem);\n        }\n\n        @ExceptionHandler(MethodArgumentNotValidException.class)\n        public ResponseEntity<ProblemDetail>   "content": "# Architectural Proposal: Data Processing Pipeline Feature\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThis document presents a comprehensive architectural proposal for implementing a new **Data Processing Pipeline** feature in the OpsForge Utility Nexus system. The feature enables users to submit complex, multi-step, asynchronous workflows that orchestrate operations across multiple utility services.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Current Architecture Summary\n\n### 1.1 Key Components and Their Roles\n\nBased on analysis of the codebase, the OpsForge Utility Nexus system consists of the following key architectural components:\n\n#### Infrastructure Components\n\n| Component | Location | Role |\n|-----------|----------|------|\n| **API Gateway** | `/app/project/api-gateway/` | Single entry-point exposing REST & GraphQL facades; handles cross-cutting concerns (rate-limiting, circuit-breaking, correlation-id propagation, routing) |\n| **Service Discovery** | `/app/project/service-discovery/` | Eureka-based service registry enabling dynamic service location (see `ServiceDiscoveryApplication.java:70-320`) |\n| **Config Server** | `/app/project/config-server/` | Spring Cloud Config Server providing centralized, versioned configuration to all microservices (see `ConfigServerApplication.java:48-225`) |\n| **Common Library** | `/app/project/common-library/` | Shared kernel containing cross-cutting concerns: logging, error responses, security utilities |\n\n#### Utility Microservices\n\n| Service | Location | Purpose |\n|---------|----------|---------|\n| **File Converter Service** | `/app/project/utility-services/file-converter-service/` | Format conversion (PDF, DOCX, CSV, JSON, etc.) |\n| **Data Anonymizer Service** | `/app/project/utility-services/data-anonymizer-service/` | PII anonymization for JSON and CSV data |\n| **Checksum Generator Service** | `/app/project/utility-services/checksum-generator-service/` | Cryptographic hash generation |\n| **Scheduler Service** | `/app/project/utility-services/scheduler-service/` | Time-zone aware scheduling |\n| **Text Transformer Service** | `/app/project/utility-services/text-transformer-service/` | Bulk text transformations |\n\n### 1.2 Architectural Patterns in Use\n\n#### Microservices Architecture (ADR-001)\nAs documented in `/app/project/docs/adr/001-architectural-style-microservices.md`:\n- Each utility is an independent, deployable microservice\n- Services own their hexagonal architecture internals\n- Communication through well-defined, versioned REST contracts\n- Domain events published for eventual consistency\n\n#### Hexagonal Architecture (ADR-002)\nAs documented in `/app/project/docs/adr/002-hexagonal-architecture-for-services.md`, each service follows the Ports & Adapters pattern:\n\n```\nService Structure (e.g., file-converter-service):\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 adapter/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 in/\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 web/           # Inbound REST adapter (FileConversionController.java)\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 messaging/     # Inbound Kafka adapter (FileConversionMessageListener.java)\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 out/\n\u2502       \u251c\u2500\u2500 persistence/   # Outbound JPA adapter\n\u2502       \u251c\u2500\u2500 cache/         # Outbound Caffeine adapter\n\u2502       \u2514\u2500\u2500 monitoring/    # Outbound metrics adapter\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 domain/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 model/             # Domain entities (ConversionRequest, ConversionResult)\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 port/\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 in/            # Inbound ports (FileConversionUseCase.java)\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 out/           # Outbound ports (ConversionAuditPort, MetricsEmitterPort)\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 service/           # Domain services (FileConversionService.java)\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 config/                # Spring configuration (BeanConfiguration.java)\n```\n\n#### API Facade Strategy (ADR-003)\nAs documented in `/app/project/docs/adr/003-api-facade-strategy.md`:\n- Unified Java-based facade using Spring Boot 3.2 + WebFlux\n- API versioning through URI segments (`/v{n}/...`)\n- Cross-cutting filters for auth, rate-limiting, metrics, caching\n\n### 1.3 Current Communication Patterns\n\nThe system currently supports two communication patterns:\n\n#### 1.3.1 Synchronous REST Communication\n- Primary pattern for client-facing interactions\n- API Gateway routes requests to downstream services via `GatewayRouteConfig.java:58-131`\n- Each service exposes REST endpoints (e.g., `FileConversionController.java:44-174`)\n- Circuit breakers and rate limiting applied at gateway level\n\n**Example Flow (File Conversion)**:\n```\nClient \u2192 API Gateway (/api/v1/convert/**)\n       \u2192 FILE-CONVERSION-SERVICE (lb://FILE-CONVERSION-SERVICE)\n       \u2192 FileConversionController.convertFile()\n       \u2192 FileConversionUseCase.convert()\n       \u2192 Response\n```\n\n#### 1.3.2 Asynchronous Messaging (Kafka)\n- Used for long-running operations and event-driven workflows\n- `FileConversionMessageListener.java:51-249` demonstrates:\n  - Kafka listener for async conversion requests\n  - Idempotency via Caffeine-based deduplication cache\n  - Result publication to dedicated reply topic\n  - Manual acknowledgment for at-least-once delivery\n\n**Evidence from codebase**:\n```java\n// FileConversionMessageListener.java:92-99\n@KafkaListener(\n    topics = \"${nexus.messaging.topics.file-conversion-requests}\",\n    groupId = \"${spring.kafka.consumer.group-id}\",\n    containerFactory = \"kafkaListenerContainerFactory\"\n)\npublic void onMessage(final ConsumerRecord<String, String> record,\n                      final Acknowledgment ack,\n                      final Consumer<?, ?> consumer) { ... }\n```\n\n---\n\n## 2. Proposal: Pipeline Orchestrator Service\n\n### 2.1 Architectural Trade-off Analysis: Orchestration vs. Choreography\n\nFor implementing multi-step workflows, two primary patterns exist:\n\n#### Choreography Pattern\n\n**How it works**: Services react to events autonomously. Each service publishes an event upon completion, and the next service in the chain subscribes to that event.\n\n**Example Flow (Anonymize \u2192 Convert)**:\n```\nClient \u2192 Anonymizer Service \u2192 publishes \"AnonymizationComplete\" event\n                            \u2192 File Converter subscribes \u2192 processes \u2192 publishes \"ConversionComplete\"\n                            \u2192 Client polls or receives callback\n```\n\n**Pros**:\n- Loose coupling between services\n- Services remain autonomous\n- Easy to add new event consumers\n\n**Cons**:\n- **Implicit workflow**: The overall process is distributed across services, making it hard to understand and debug\n- **State management**: No central place to track job progress; each service only knows its part\n- **Error handling complexity**: If step 2 of 3 fails, implementing compensation/rollback is challenging\n- **Monitoring difficulty**: Requires correlation IDs and distributed tracing to follow a job's path\n\n#### Orchestration Pattern (Recommended)\n\n**How it works**: A central orchestrator explicitly manages the workflow, calling each service in sequence and maintaining job state.\n\n**Example Flow (Anonymize \u2192 Convert)**:\n```\nClient \u2192 Pipeline Orchestrator Service\n       \u2192 (1) Calls Anonymizer Service \u2192 stores intermediate result\n       \u2192 (2) Calls File Converter Service \u2192 stores final result\n       \u2192 Updates job state at each step\n       \u2192 Client polls for status/result\n```\n\n**Pros**:\n- **Explicit workflow**: The entire process is visible in one place\n- **Centralized state**: Job progress, status, and results are managed uniformly\n- **Error handling**: Clear location for retries, compensation, and failure logging\n- **Monitoring**: Single service exposes job status, making dashboards straightforward\n- **Extensibility**: Easy to add new steps, conditional logic, or parallel execution\n\n**Cons**:\n- Orchestrator is tightly coupled to workflow logic\n- Single point of failure (mitigated by standard resilience patterns)\n\n### 2.2 Recommendation: Orchestration\n\nFor a **defined, stateful, multi-step business process** like the Data Processing Pipeline, **orchestration is the superior pattern**. The explicit nature of the workflow, combined with the need for robust state management and error handling, makes a central orchestrator the right choice.\n\n### 2.3 Proposed Solution: New `pipeline-orchestrator-service`\n\n#### Why a New Service?\n\n1. **Separation of Concerns**: Pipeline orchestration is a distinct capability from the individual utilities\n2. **Bounded Context**: The pipeline domain (jobs, steps, state transitions) is separate from conversion/anonymization domains\n3. **Scalability**: The orchestrator can scale independently based on pipeline job volume\n4. **Consistency**: Follows the existing pattern where each capability is a separate microservice\n\n#### Service Architecture\n\nThe new service will follow the established Hexagonal Architecture:\n\n```\npipeline-orchestrator-service/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 src/main/java/com/opsforge/nexus/pipeline/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 adapter/\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 in/\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 web/\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2502       \u251c\u2500\u2500 PipelineController.java          # REST endpoints\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2502       \u2514\u2500\u2500 dto/\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2502           \u251c\u2500\u2500 CreatePipelineJobRequest.java\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2502           \u251c\u2500\u2500 PipelineJobStatusResponse.java\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2502           \u2514\u2500\u2500 PipelineStepDto.java\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 out/\n\u2502   \u2502       \u251c\u2500\u2500 persistence/\n\u2502   \u2502       \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 JpaPipelineJobRepository.java    # PostgreSQL adapter\n\u2502   \u2502       \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 entity/\n\u2502   \u2502       \u2502       \u251c\u2500\u2500 PipelineJobEntity.java\n\u2502   \u2502       \u2502       \u2514\u2500\u2500 PipelineStepEntity.java\n\u2502   \u2502       \u2514\u2500\u2500 service/\n\u2502   \u2502           \u251c\u2500\u2500 AnonymizerServiceClient.java     # HTTP client adapter\n\u2502   \u2502           \u251c\u2500\u2500 FileConverterServiceClient.java  # HTTP client adapter\n\u2502   \u2502           \u2514\u2500\u2500 ChecksumServiceClient.java       # HTTP client adapter\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 domain/\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 model/\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 PipelineJob.java                     # Aggregate root\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 PipelineStep.java                    # Value object\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 JobStatus.java                       # Enum\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 StepDefinition.java                  # Step configuration\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 port/\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 in/\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 PipelineOrchestrationUseCase.java  # Inbound port\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 out/\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2502       \u251c\u2500\u2500 PipelineJobRepository.java        # Outbound port\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2502       \u251c\u2500\u2500 AnonymizerPort.java               # Outbound port\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2502       \u2514\u2500\u2500 FileConverterPort.java            # Outbound port\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 service/\n\u2502   \u2502       \u2514\u2500\u2500 PipelineOrchestrationService.java    # Domain service\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 config/\n\u2502       \u251c\u2500\u2500 BeanConfiguration.java\n\u2502       \u2514\u2500\u2500 AsyncConfig.java\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 src/main/resources/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 application.yml\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 bootstrap.yml\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 pom.xml\n```\n\n---\n\n## 3. Detailed Data Flow: Anonymize-then-Convert Pipeline\n\n### 3.1 End-to-End Flow Diagram\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510 \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u25b6\n```\n\n### 3.2 Step-by-Step Description\n\n#### Step 1: Client Submits Pipeline Job\n\n**Request**:\n```http\nPOST /api/v1/pipelines/jobs\nHost: api-gateway:8080\nContent-Type: application/json\nAuthorization: Bearer <jwt-token>\nX-Correlation-Id: abc-123\n\n{\n  \"name\": \"customer-data-processing\",\n  \"steps\": [\n    {\n      \"type\": \"ANONYMIZE\",\n      \"config\": {\n        \"rules\": {\n          \"email\": \"MASK\",\n          \"phone\": \"HASH\",\n          \"ssn\": \"NULLIFY\"\n        }\n      }\n    },\n    {\n      \"type\": \"CONVERT\",\n      \"config\": {\n        \"targetFormat\": \"PARQUET\"\n      }\n    }\n  ],\n  \"inputData\": {\n    \"sourceType\": \"INLINE\",\n    \"format\": \"CSV\",\n    \"content\": \"base64-encoded-csv-data\"\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**Response** (Immediate):\n```http\nHTTP/1.1 202 Accepted\nLocation: /api/v1/pipelines/jobs/job-uuid-12345\nX-Correlation-Id: abc-123\n\n{\n  \"jobId\": \"job-uuid-12345\",\n  \"status\": \"PENDING\",\n  \"createdAt\": \"2024-01-15T10:30:00Z\",\n  \"steps\": [\n    { \"stepIndex\": 0, \"type\": \"ANONYMIZE\", \"status\": \"PENDING\" },\n    { \"stepIndex\": 1, \"type\": \"CONVERT\", \"status\": \"PENDING\" }\n  ]\n}\n```\n\n#### Step 2: Orchestrator Executes Anonymization\n\nThe orchestrator (running asynchronously via `@Async` executor):\n\n1. **Updates job state** to `IN_PROGRESS`\n2. **Updates step 0 state** to `IN_PROGRESS`\n3. **Calls Anonymizer Service**:\n   ```http\n   POST /api/v1/anonymizer/json\n   Host: data-anonymizer-service:8091\n   X-Correlation-Id: abc-123\n\n   {\n     \"payload\": { ... csv as json ... },\n     \"rules\": { \"email\": \"MASK\", \"phone\": \"HASH\", \"ssn\": \"NULLIFY\" }\n   }\n   ```\n4. **Stores intermediate result** (anonymized data) in object storage or database\n5. **Updates step 0 state** to `COMPLETED`\n\n#### Step 3: Orchestrator Executes Conversion\n\n1. **Updates step 1 state** to `IN_PROGRESS`\n2. **Retrieves intermediate result** from storage\n3. **Calls File Converter Service**:\n   ```http\n   POST /api/v1/convert\n   Host: file-converter-service:8082\n   X-Correlation-Id: abc-123\n   Content-Type: multipart/form-data\n\n   file: <anonymized-data>\n   targetFormat: PARQUET\n   ```\n4. **Stores final result** (converted file)\n5. **Updates step 1 state** to `COMPLETED`\n6. **Updates job state** to `COMPLETED`\n\n#### Step 4: Client Polls for Status\n\n**Request**:\n```http\nGET /api/v1/pipelines/jobs/job-uuid-12345\nAuthorization: Bearer <jwt-token>\n```\n\n**Response** (Completed):\n```json\n{\n  \"jobId\": \"job-uuid-12345\",\n  \"status\": \"COMPLETED\",\n  \"createdAt\": \"2024-01-15T10:30:00Z\",\n  \"completedAt\": \"2024-01-15T10:31:45Z\",\n  \"steps\": [\n    { \"stepIndex\": 0, \"type\": \"ANONYMIZE\", \"status\": \"COMPLETED\", \"duration\": \"45s\" },\n    { \"stepIndex\": 1, \"type\": \"CONVERT\", \"status\": \"COMPLETED\", \"duration\": \"60s\" }\n  ],\n  \"result\": {\n    \"downloadUrl\": \"/api/v1/pipelines/jobs/job-uuid-12345/result\",\n    \"checksum\": \"sha256:abc123...\",\n    \"sizeBytes\": 524288\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### Step 5: Client Downloads Result\n\n```http\nGET /api/v1/pipelines/jobs/job-uuid-12345/result\nAuthorization: Bearer <jwt-token>\n\nHTTP/1.1 200 OK\nContent-Type: application/octet-stream\nContent-Disposition: attachment; filename=\"customer-data-processed.parquet\"\n```\n\n### 3.3 Error Handling Flow\n\nIf step 2 (Conversion) fails:\n\n```json\n{\n  \"jobId\": \"job-uuid-12345\",\n  \"status\": \"FAILED\",\n  \"createdAt\": \"2024-01-15T10:30:00Z\",\n  \"failedAt\": \"2024-01-15T10:31:30Z\",\n  \"steps\": [\n    { \"stepIndex\": 0, \"type\": \"ANONYMIZE\", \"status\": \"COMPLETED\" },\n    {\n      \"stepIndex\": 1,\n      \"type\": \"CONVERT\",\n      \"status\": \"FAILED\",\n      \"error\": {\n        \"code\": \"UNSUPPORTED_CONVERSION\",\n        \"message\": \"Cannot convert JSON to PARQUET: schema inference failed\"\n      }\n    }\n  ]\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Key Design Decisions\n\n### 6.1 Asynchronous Job Processing\n\nJobs are processed asynchronously using Spring's `@Async` with a dedicated thread pool:\n\n```java\n@Configuration\n@EnableAsync\npublic class AsyncConfig {\n    @Bean(\"pipelineExecutor\")\n    public Executor pipelineExecutor() {\n        ThreadPoolTaskExecutor executor = new ThreadPoolTaskExecutor();\n        executor.setCorePoolSize(10);\n        executor.setMaxPoolSize(50);\n        executor.setQueueCapacity(100);\n        executor.setThreadNamePrefix(\"pipeline-\");\n        executor.initialize();\n        return executor;\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### 6.2 State Persistence\n\nJob state is persisted to PostgreSQL to survive orchestrator restarts:\n\n```sql\nCREATE TABLE pipeline_jobs (\n    id UUID PRIMARY KEY,\n    name VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,\n    status VARCHAR(50) NOT NULL,\n    created_at TIMESTAMP NOT NULL,\n    updated_at TIMESTAMP NOT NULL,\n    completed_at TIMESTAMP,\n    correlation_id VARCHAR(100),\n    input_data_ref VARCHAR(500)\n);\n\nCREATE TABLE pipeline_steps (\n    id UUID PRIMARY KEY,\n    job_id UUID REFERENCES pipeline_jobs(id),\n    step_index INT NOT NULL,\n    step_type VARCHAR(50) NOT NULL,\n    status VARCHAR(50) NOT NULL,\n    config JSONB,\n    started_at TIMESTAMP,\n    completed_at TIMESTAMP,\n    output_ref VARCHAR(500),\n    error_message TEXT\n);\n```\n\n### 6.3 Intermediate Data Storage\n\nFor intermediate results between pipeline steps:\n- Small payloads (<1MB): Store in PostgreSQL JSONB column\n- Large payloads: Store in S3-compatible object storage (MinIO in development)\n\n### 6.4 Idempotency\n\nJob creation is idempotent using client-provided `idempotencyKey`:\n\n```java\n@PostMapping(\"/jobs\")\npublic ResponseEntity<PipelineJobStatusResponse> createJob(\n    @RequestHeader(value = \"Idempotency-Key\", required = false) String idempotencyKey,\n    @RequestBody CreatePipelineJobRequest request) {\n\n    if (idempotencyKey != null) {\n        Optional<PipelineJob> existing = jobRepository.findByIdempotencyKey(idempotencyKey);\n        if (existing.isPresent()) {\n            return ResponseEntity.ok(mapToResponse(existing.get()));\n        }\n    }\n    // ... create new job\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 7. Conclusion\n\nThis architectural proposal introduces a new `pipeline-orchestrator-service` that:\n\n1. **Follows existing patterns**: Hexagonal architecture, microservices, API facade strategy\n2. **Uses orchestration over choreography**: Provides explicit, manageable, and monitorable workflows\n3. **Minimizes impact**: Only requires adding a new service module and updating gateway routes\n4. **Enables extensibility**: Easy to add new step types, conditional logic, or parallel execution\n\nThe solution leverages the existing infrastructure (Service Discovery, Config Server, API Gateway) while introducing workflow orchestration as a first-class capability.\n\n---\n\n## References\n\n- ADR-001: `/app/project/docs/adr/001-architectural-style-microservices.md`\n- ADR-002: `/app/project/docs/adr/002-hexagonal-architecture-for-services.md`\n- ADR-003: `/app/project/docs/adr/003-api-facade-strategy.md`\n- File Converter Service: `/app/project/utility-services/file-converter-service/`\n- Data Anonymizer Service: `/app/project/utility-services/data-anonymizer-service/`\n- API Gateway Routes: `/app/project/api-gateway/src/main/java/com/opsforge/nexus/gateway/config/GatewayRouteConfig.java`\n- Docker Compose: `/app/project/docker-compose.yml`\n",
